acf_elev_trim_speedratfloat825+yesratioThis is the speed of trim time, expressed as a ratio, where 1.0 means it takes 20 seconds to fully move trim from one extreme to the other. 2.0 means trim is twice as fast.

acf_elev_def_timefloat1000+yessecsEnter 0.0 to be able to deflect the controls as fast as the pilot can move the stick or the art stab system can command a deflection. If the plane has a hydraulic system and a max rate of control deflection, though, enter how long it takes to go from center to fully-deflected.

If the plane has a hydraulic system and a max rate of control deflection, though, enter how long it takes to go from center to fully-deflected.

sim/cockpit/warnings/

Caution and warnings are masters for annunciators by type. Master accept is lit for any warning or caution, so it is a catch-all. Use warnings/annunciators to see if the indicator is lit. Use the command-system to actuate changes to the annunciators.

ECAM_warning_onint660-922yesbooelanIs there a warning lit on the ECAM

master_warning_onfloat930+yesbooleanMaster warning is enabled for being lit (because it is not pressed)
master_accept_onfloat660+yesbooleanMaster accept is enabled for being lit (because it is not pressed)

sim/operation/g430/

These datarefs only apply to real, physical G430s, e.g. if you buy an expensive G430 and plug it into your PC! This is not for any _simulated_ system.

G430_is_vlocint[2]1030+nobooleanIf true, vertical guidance is a glide slope – otherwise it is a GPS vertical guidance indicator. Comes from the physical units!
sim/operation/misc/

debug_networkint660+yesbooleanEnable logging of network data
frame_rate_periodfloat660+yessecsThe frame rate period. Use the reciprocal to get the frame rate (e.g. 1/mnw.prd). Writable via override_timestep in 11.10
time_ratiofloat660+nosecsThis is how close XP time matches real time. Ideal ratio is 1. NOTE: in 930 and later time ratio is always 1.0.

sim/aircraft2/

This section contains dataref access to the aircraft that has been auditied by LR for maintenance. Unlike sim/aircraft/, if you can write these datarefs, it is safe to do so, and reading these datarefs makes sense.

sim/aircraft2/metadata/

This section contains read-only views of some of the current user’s aircraft meta-data.

is_ultralightint1130+noBoolean1 if the vehicle is categorized as an ultralight, 0 if it is not.

is_general_aviationint1130+noBoolean1 if the vehicle is categorized as a general aviation aircraft, 0 if it is not.
is_airlinerint1130+noBoolean1 if the vehicle is categorized as an airliner, 0 if it is not.
is_militaryint1130+noBoolean1 if the vehicle is categorized as a military aircraft, 0 if it is not.
is_cargoint1130+noBoolean1 if the vehicle is categorized as a cargo aircraft, 0 if it is not.
is_gliderint1130+noBoolean1 if the vehicle is categorized as a glider, 0 if it is not.
is_seaplaneint1130+noBoolean1 if the vehicle is categorized as a seaplane, 0 if it is not.
is_helicopterint1130+noBoolean1 if the vehicle is categorized as a helicopter, 0 if it is not.
is_vtolint1130+noBoolean1 if the vehicle is categorized as a VTOL, 0 if it is not.

sim/cockpit2/

This section contains datarefs useful for custom cockpits. Typically data is broken into indicators (what the pilot sees via instruments) and actuators (write to these to change what the plane does). The actuators may not work when a failure happens, and the indicators may show false readings. By using these datarefs, your cockpit will match the failure settings.

sim/cockpit2/annunciators/

Annunciators, all are essentially indications.

master_cautionint900+nobooleanThis goes off any time there is a major problem with the bird: like it is on fire or something // array of annunciators… kept as array for UDP IO
master_warningint900+nobooleanThis goes off whenever there is some more moderate problem with the bird… maybe lo fuel pressure ot qty
master_acceptint900+nobooleanHit this button to CLEAR the master caution and warning: it says that you hear the buzzer and to shut it up already
autopilot_disconnectint900+nobooleanThis goes off for a few moments when the autopilot disconnects.. you wanna KNOW if otto just quit on you!
low_vacuumint900+nobooleanThe vacuum pressure, which drives the instruments in the old prop planes, is low: the artificial horizon may loose it is orientation!
low_voltageint900+nobooleanThe voltage os too high or low on one of the electrical buses
fuel_quantityint900+nobooleanFuel qty. no points for guessing if it is too high or too low to trigger this one
hydraulic_pressureint900+nobooleanHydraulic pressure. should indicate if press is lo or hi
speedbrakeint900+nobooleanSpeedbrake deployed: good to know so you do not forget it..
GPWSint900+nobooleanGround proximity warning system: PULL UP! PULL UP! my lancair does this during my typical red-baron approaches!
iceint900+nobooleanIce detected on the plane.. most people agree this is NOT a good thing.
low_rotorint900+nobooleanRotor rpm on the helo has dropped below normal operating: power availability will be reduced!
high_rotorint900+nobooleanRotor rpm on the helo has exceeded normal operating: power availability will be reduced, and god knows if the blades will stay ON!

sim/cockpit2/ice/

Actuators for ice switches

ice_all_onint900+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – all systems. This is the master switch for the de-icing systems.
ice_inlet_heat_onint900+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – inlet heat. This switch turns on de-icing heat in the engine air inlet keep ice from choking your engine. Engine 1 only
ice_prop_heat_onint900+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – prop heat. This switch turns on de-icing of the propeller(s) to keep ice from building up on your prop. Engine 1 only
ice_inlet_heat_on_per_engineint[8]1020+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – inlet heat. This switch turns on de-icing heat in the engine air inlet keep ice from choking your engine. Per engine
ice_prop_heat_on_per_engineint[8]1020+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – prop heat. This switch turns on de-icing of the propeller(s) to keep ice from building up on your prop. Per engine
ice_window_heat_onint900+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – windshield heat. This switch turns on windshield de-icing to keep ice from blocking your vision.
ice_pitot_heat_on_pilotint900+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – pitot tube heat. This switch turns on de-icing heat in the pitot tube. If it freezes up your airspeed indicator and altimeter stop working. Airspeed and altitude related autopilot functions are also affected.
ice_pitot_heat_on_copilotint900+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. Pitot tube heat, co-pilot. This switch turns on de-icing heat in the co-pilot side pitot tube. If it freezes up your airspeed indicator and altimeter stop working. Airspeed and altitude related autopilot functions are also affected.
ice_AOA_heat_onint900+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. AOA sensor heat. This switch turns on de-icing heat for the AOA sensor. If it freezes up your AOA indicator stops working. AOA sensor failure will also affect the aircraft’s artificial stability system if it has one. Pilot.
ice_AOA_heat_on_copilotint1020+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. AOA sensor heat. This switch turns on de-icing heat for the AOA sensor. If it freezes up your AOA indicator stops working. AOA sensor failure will also affect the aircraft’s artificial stability system if it has one. Copilot.
ice_static_heat_on_pilotint1120+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. Static port heat. This switch turns on de-icing heat for the static sensor. If it freezes up your altimeter, vvi and airspeed indicator stop working. Pilot.
ice_static_heat_on_copilotint1120+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. Static port heat. This switch turns on de-icing heat for the static sensor. If it freezes up your altimeter, vvi and airspeed indicator stop working. Copilot.
ice_surfce_heat_onint900+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – electric heat. This switch engages electrically heated leading edges. (All wings)
ice_surfce_heat_left_onint930+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – electric heat. This switch engages electrically heated leading edges. (Left wing)
ice_surfce_heat_right_onint930+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – electric heat. This switch engages electrically heated leading edges. (Right wing)
ice_surface_boot_onint900-1129yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – pneumatic. This switch inflates flexible bladders on the wing leading edges to pop off accumulated ice.
ice_surface_boot_onint1130+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – pneumatic. This switch inflates flexible bladders on the wing leading edges to pop off accumulated ice. (All wings)
ice_surface_boot_left_onint1130+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – pneumatic. This switch inflates flexible bladders on the wing leading edges to pop off accumulated ice. (Left wing)
ice_surface_boot_right_onint1130+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – pneumatic. This switch inflates flexible bladders on the wing leading edges to pop off accumulated ice. (Right wing)
ice_surface_hot_bleed_air_onint1130+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – bleed air. This switch directs warm air from the engines into the wing leading edges to keep them free of ice. (All wings)
ice_surface_hot_bleed_air_left_onint1130+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – bleed air. This switch directs warm air from the engines into the wing leading edges to keep them free of ice. (Left wing)
ice_surface_hot_bleed_air_right_onint1130+yesbooleanDe-ice switch, 0 or 1. De-ice – bleed air. This switch directs warm air from the engines into the wing leading edges to keep them free of ice. (Right wing)

ice_surface_tks_right_onint1130+yesenumDe-ice switch, 0, 1, or 2. De-ice – TKS fluid. This switch activates the pump for the weeping wing, dissipating TKS fluid on the leading edges to keep them free of ice. 0 = Off, 1 = Norm, 2 = High. (Right wing)

tcas_num_acfint1150+nointegerIf TCAS is not overriden by plgugin, returns the number of planes in X-Plane, which might be under plugin control or X-Plane control. If TCAS is overriden, returns how many targets are actually being written to with the override. These are not necessarily consecutive entries in the TCAS arrays.

sim/flightmodel2/

The flightmodel2 section contains data about how the actual aircraft is being drawn. Use this section to build animated objects for the aircraft. Do not use these datarefs in the cockpit.

sim/flightmodel2/controls/

This section contains general control surface values for the whole plane. These are the actual control movements, e.g. if the control efficacy is reduced by low hydraulic pressure, these show what actually moved, not what the pilot wants.

pitch_ratiofloat900+yesratioThis is how much the flight controls are deflected in pitch after any stability augmentation, in ratio, where -1.0 is full down, and 1.0 is full up.
roll_ratiofloat900+yesratioThis is how much the flight controls are deflected in roll after any stability augmentation, in ratio, where -1.0 is full left, and 1.0 is full right.
heading_ratiofloat900+yesratioThis is how much the flight controls are deflected in heading after any stability augmentation, where -1.0 is full left, and 1.0 is full right.
speedbrake_ratiofloat900+yesratioThis is how much the speedbrakes surfaces are extended, in ratio, where 0.0 is fully retracted, and 1.0 is fully extended.
wingsweep_ratiofloat900+yesratioActual sweep, in ratio. 0.0 is no sweep deployment, 1 is max sweep deployment.
thrust_vector_ratiofloat900+yesratioActual thrust vector, in ratio. 0.0 is no thrust vector deployment, 1 is max thrust vector deployment.
dihedral_ratiofloat900+yesratioActual dihedral, in ratio. 0.0 is no dihedral deployment, 1 is max dihedral deployment.
incidence_ratiofloat900+yesratioActual incidence, in ratio. 0.0 is no incidence deployment, 1 is max incidence deployment.
wing_retraction_ratiofloat900+yesratioActual wing-retraction, in ratio. 0.0 is no wing-retraction deployment, 1 is max wing-retraction deployment.
flap_handle_deploy_ratiofloat900+yesratioThis is the ACTUAL FLAP deployment for overall flap system, in ratio, where 0.0 is flaps fully retracted, and 1.0 is flaps fully extended. You should probably use the deployment for flap set 1 or flap set 2 to deflect the surfaces though. This takes into account that flaps deploy slowly, not instantaneously as the handle is dragged.
slat1_deploy_ratiofloat900+yesratioSlat deployment, where 0.0 is slats fully retracted, 1.0 is slats fully extended. This variable applies to lading-edge flaps as well.
slat2_deploy_ratiofloat900+yesratioSlat deployment, where 0.0 is slats fully retracted, 1.0 is slats fully extended. This variable applies to lading-edge flaps as well.
flap1_deploy_ratiofloat900+yesratioThis is the ACTUAL FLAP deployment for flap-set #1, in ratio, where 0.0 is flaps fully retracted, and 1.0 is flaps fully extended.
flap2_deploy_ratiofloat900+yesratioThis is the ACTUAL FLAP deployment for flap-set #2, in ratio, where 0.0 is flaps fully retracted, and 1.0 is flaps fully extended.
stabilizer_deflection_degreesfloat900+yesdegreesThis is the actual stabilizer deflection with trim for all-moving horizontal stabilizers. This is the deflection you can see visually on airliners. This is in degrees, positive for leading-edge nose up.
aileron_trimfloat900+yesratioAileron trim, in part of MAX FLIGHT CONTROL DEFLECTION. So, if the aileron trim is deflected enough to move the ailerons through 30% of their travel, then that is an aileron trim of 0.3.
elevator_trimfloat900+yesratioElevator trim, in part of MAX FLIGHT CONTROL DEFLECTION. So, if the elevator trim is deflected enough to move the elevators through 30% of their travel, then that is an elevator trim of 0.3.
rudder_trimfloat900+yesratioRudder trim, in part of MAX FLIGHT CONTROL DEFLECTION. So, if the rudder trim is deflected enough to move the rudders through 30% of their travel, then that is an rudder trim of 0.3.
rotor_trimfloat900+yesratioRotor trim, in part of MAX FLIGHT CONTROL DEFLECTION. So, if the rotor trim is deflected enough to move the rotor through 30% of its travel, then that is a rotor trim of 0.3.
water_rudder_deploy_ratiofloat901+noratioDeployment of the water rudder, 0 is none, 1 is max

Landing gear doors.

typeint[doors]900+noenumeration0=unused (plane does not use this door) 1=standard (opens before gear goes down) 2=attached to strut (cycles with door), 3=closed (opens before gear goes down, then closes again)
location_x_mtrint[doors]900-1099nometersGear door location, in meters, x, y z.
location_y_mtrint[doors]900-1099nometersGear door location, in meters, x, y z.
location_z_mtrint[doors]900-1099nometersGear door location, in meters, x, y z.
axis_rotation_degfloat[doors]900-1099nodegreesAxis of rotation of this gear door, degrees.
angle_now_degfloat[doors]900+nodegreesCurrent angle about the axis of rotation of this gear door, degrees.
sim/flightmodel2/engines/

Datarefs for the physical engines, props and rotors.

location_x_mtrfloat[engines]900+nometersEngine location, meters x, y, z, with respect to the default center of gravity.
location_y_mtrfloat[engines]900+nometersEngine location, meters x, y, z, with respect to the default center of gravity.
location_z_mtrfloat[engines]900+nometersEngine location, meters x, y, z, with respect to the default center of gravity.
throttle_used_ratiofloat[engines]900+noratioThrottle that is actually going to the engine, which could be different than the commanded throttle due to FADEC throttle adjustments.
has_fuel_flow_before_mixtureint[8]900+yesbooleanEngine has fuel making to the mixture control, yes or no. Writable if override_fuel_system is true.
has_fuel_flow_after_mixtureint[engines]900+nobooleanEngine has fuel making to the combustion process, yes or no.
engine_is_burning_fuelint[engines]900+nobooleanEngine is currently burning fuel, yes or no.
engine_fuel_in_intakefloat[engines]1031+noratioHow much fuel has been primed into the intake port (fuel-injected engine) 0..1
engine_burning_fuel_ratioint[engines]900-902noratioEngine running ratio, 0.0 for not running to 1.0 for fully running, combustion process fully started.
afterburner_onint[engines]900+nobooleanAfterburner on, yes or no.
afterburner_ratiofloat[engines]900+noratioAfterburner engaged ratio, 0.0 to 1.0.
engine_rotation_speed_rad_secfloat[engines]900+noradians/secondRotational speed of the engine, in radians per second.
engine_rotation_angle_degfloat[engines]900+nodegreesThis is the angle of the engine as it turns over, running 0 to 360 over and over again in normal operation. Engine speed can be different than prop rotation speed in clutched designs. This is radians per second.
prop_rotation_speed_rad_secfloat[engines]900+noradians/secondRadians per second rotation speed of the prop.
prop_rotation_angle_degfloat[engines]900+yesdegreesThis is the angle of the prop or engine-fan as it rotates. You will see this value circulate 0 to 360 degrees over and over as the engine runs and the prop or fan turns. Override witih /prop_disc/override per engine!
prop_no_disc_rotation_angle_degfloat[engines]1050+nodegreesThis is the angle of the prop or engine-fan as it rotates. You will see this value circulate 0 to 360 degrees over and over as the engine runs and the prop or fan turns. This dataref NEVER shows the speed of the prop disc if it happens to be showing. This always tracks the actual prop. Override witih /prop_disc/override per engine!
prop_pitch_degfloat[engines]900+nodegreesThis is the ACTUAL pitch of the prop in degrees from its flat-pitch setting.
prop_cone_angle_radfloat[engines]900+noradiansThis is the coning angle of the disc, in radians. Typically close to 0.0.
rotor_vertical_vector_degfloat[engines]900+nodegreesThis engine rotor-disc vertical vector, in degrees, where 0 is straight forwards, 90 is straight up.
rotor_vertical_cyclic_degfloat[engines]900+nodegreesThis engine rotor-disc longitudinal cyclic, in degrees, where -10 is 10 degrees forwards, 10 is 10 degrees aft.
rotor_side_cyclic_degfloat[engines]900+nodegreesThis engine rotor-disc lateral cyclic, in degrees, where -10 is 10 degrees left, 10 is 10 degrees right.
rotor_cyclic_elevator_tilt_degfloat[engines]900+nodegreesLongitudinal disc tilt from cyclic deflection.
rotor_cyclic_aileron_tilt_degfloat[engines]900+nodegreesLateral disc tilt from cyclic deflection.
nacelle_vertical_angle_degfloat[engines]900+nodegreesThis engine nacelle vertical vector, in degrees, where 0 is straight forwards, 90 is straight up.
thrust_reverser_deploy_ratiofloat[engines]900+noratioHow far the reverser doors/mechanism have traveled. 0 = fully stowed, 1.0 = fully deployed.
prop_is_discint[engines]930+yesbooleanIs the prop a disc now? Override with /prop_disc/override per engine!
prop_tip_deflection_degreesfloat[8]1000+nodegreesDegrees of deflection of a line from the crank shaft to the prop tip.
fuel_pump_spinningfloat[engines]1050+no0..1Is the electric fuel pump for this engine spinning? 1 = yes, 0 = no.
starter_is_runningint[8]1100+nobooleanIs this starter running at all
starter_making_torqueint[8]1100+nobooleanIs this starter applying torque to the engine
is_on_firefloat[8]1130+no0..1Engine fire, 0 means none, 1 means max.
side_signfloat[8]1130+no-1,0,1Sign of the side of the ACF for this engine: -1 for left side, 0 for inline, 1 for right side
N1_percentfloat[engines]1130+nopercentN1 speed as percent of max (per engine)
N2_percentfloat[engines]1130+nopercentN2 speed as percent of max (per engine)
ITT_deg_Cfloat[engines]1130+nodegreesITT (per engine) in degrees C
EGT_deg_Cfloat[engines]1130+nodegreesEGT (per engine) in degrees C
CHT_deg_Cfloat[engines]1130+nodegreesCHT (per engine) in degrees C
jetwash_mtr_secfloat[engines]1130+nometers/secondSpeed of propwash/jetwash behind the prop disc/engine exhaust in meters/second

sim/flightmodel2/wing/

Wing properties. These give you the most specific access to control surfaces (for example, these include variable flaps with roll and pitch). The wings are indexed as: wing 1 left, wing 1 right .. wing 4 left, wing 4 right, left hstab, right hstab, rudders 1 and 2, then the 20 misc wings, for 32 indices.

aileron1_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the aileron from set #1 on this wing. Degrees, positive is trailing-edge down.
aileron2_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the aileron from set #2 on this wing. Degrees, positive is trailing-edge down.
spoiler1_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the roll-spoilerfrom set #1 on this wing. Degrees, positive is trailing-edge down.
spoiler2_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the roll-spoilerfrom set #1 on this wing. Degrees, positive is trailing-edge down.
yawbrake_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the yaw-brake on this wing. A yaw-brake is a set of spoilers on the top and bottom of the wing that split open symmetrically to drag that wing aft and yaw the plane. They are used on the B-2, for example.
elevator1_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the elevator from set #1 on this wing. Degrees, positive is trailing-edge down.
elevator2_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the elevator from set #2 on this wing. Degrees, positive is trailing-edge down.
rudder1_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the rudder from set #1 on this wing. Degrees, positive is trailing-edge right.
rudder2_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the rudder from set #2 on this wing. Degrees, positive is trailing-edge right.
flap1_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the flap from set #1 on this wing. Degrees, positive is trailing-edge down.
flap2_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the flap from set #2 on this wing. Degrees, positive is trailing-edge down.
speedbrake1_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the speedbrakes from set #1 on this wing.
speedbrake2_degfloat[wings]900+yesdegreesDeflection of the speedbrakes from set #2 on this wing.
airfoil_sweep_increase_degfloat[wings]900-999yesdegreesThe sweep increase BEYOND DEFAULT of this wing… this would only have a non-zero value for planes like the F-14 which can sweep their wings.
airfoil_dihedral_increase_degfloat[wings]900-999yesdegreesThe dihedral increase BEYOND DEFAULT of this wing… this would only have a non-zero value for planes like the Navy F-4 which can fold up the outer wing panels.
wing_tip_deflection_degfloat[32]1000+nodegreesDegrees of deflection of a line from the wing root (extended to the plane centerline) to the tip.
wing_condensation_ratiofloat[wings]1130+noratioStrength of wing condensation for this wing, 0 is none, 1 = max
wing_tip_condensation_ratiofloat[wings]1130+noratioStrength of wing tip vapor trail for this wing, 0 is none, 1 = max
sim/flightmodel2/wing/elements/

Per-element data, 10 per wing x 32 wings.

element_MAC_mtrfloat[320]1130+nometersWidth of chord at the MAC.
element_surface_area_mtr_sqfloat[320]1130+nosquare_metersper element surface area
element_condensation_ratiofloat[320]1130+noratioPer element condensation ratio
element_is_stalledfloat[320]1140+nobooleanPer element – is this element stalled?
sim/graphics/VR/

Controller animation values – these are used to animate controllers using OBJs.

Controller animation values – these are used to animate controllers using OBJs.

button_axis_xfloat[5]1120+noRatioFor OBJs used to draw VR controllers: the X deflection (or axis deflection) of each axis on the controller.
button_axis_yfloat[5]1120+noRatioFor OBJs used to draw VR controllers: for 2-d thumb sticks or dpads, this is the second axis.
button_downint[64]1120+noBooleanFor OBJs used to draw VR controllers: button status of each button on the controller.
backlight_levelfloat1120+noRatioFor OBJs used to draw VR controllers: Level of back lighting on the controller.
seeker_light_levelfloat1120+noRatioFor OBJs used to draw VR controllers: Level of lighting on the tip of the controller.
touch_spot_light_levelfloat1120+noRatioFor OBJs used to draw VR controllers: Level of lighting on the D-Pad/joystick part of the controller.
enabledint1120+noBooleanTrue if VR is enabled, false if it is disabled
using_3d_mouseint1120+noBooleanTrue if the 3-d VR mouse is in use
teleport_on_groundint1120+noBooleanTrue if the user is teleporting outside the aircraft. In this case the pilot’s head position is not reliable – use the regular camera location
